**8-38** **(1/12/14) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|ICr.50.4<br>a)<br>the potential effects of any increase of radiofrequency exposure on the<br>health of persons near the facility.<br>b)<br>the nature of any activities near the proposed site, having regard to their<br>susceptibility to any exposures.<br>c)<br>the location of the site, and any potential for shielding from exposures.<br>d)<br>any cumulative effects, particularly with regard to exposure to electro<br>magnetic radiation from existing facilities in the area.|ICr.50.5<br>Certain utilities and other activities emit electromagnetic radiation.<br>These activities are perceived to be a health concern to some people<br>living near them.<br>In developing the rules on radiofrequency exposures, Council has<br>based its approach on that recommended in the “National Guidelines<br>for Managing the Effects of Radiofrequency Transmitters” produced<br>by the Ministry of Health and the Ministry for the Environment in<br>December 2000.  The key findings of the guidelines was that there<br>are no established health effects from exposure to radiofrequency<br>fields as long as they comply with the New Zealand Standard NZS<br>2772.1:1999 Radiofrequency Fields: Part 1 – Maximum Exposure<br>Levels 3kHz-300GHz.<br>The Council is to be notified of location and nature of any proposed<br>facility.  Should this predictive report anticipate and should exposure<br>levels be greater than 25 percent of the New Zealand Standard level,<br>monitoring to determine the actual exposure levels from the<br>transmitting installation will be required.<br>The rule contains an exception for domestic radiofrequency<br>transmitting equipment.  This is to ensure that these domestic<br>transmitting devices can be used without the rules applying to their<br>radiofrequency emissions.<br>Radiofrequency emissions that exceed the exposure levels set within<br>the New Zealand Standard are to be considered as non-complying<br>activities.|
|ICr.51.4<br>a)<br>any hazard presented by the utility.<br>b)<br>the environmental setting of the structure, having regard to the general<br>locality, topography, geographical features and adjacent land uses.<br>c)<br>the visual impacts of the structure on residential or recreational use of land<br>in the vicinity, and on significant ridge lines and view planes from public places,<br>including roads.<br>d)<br>the scale, bulk and height of the facility.<br>e)<br>screening or landscaping of the utility and any modifications to its colour<br>and design to reduce the visual effect of the utility on the surrounding<br>environment.<br>f)<br>any constraints on placing the utility underground.|<br>ICr.51.5<br>Provision is made for lower pressure gas lines as permitted activities,<br>but high pressure lines which present a higher risk need to be<br>assessed as discretionary activities.<br>The electricity and telephone network is an important part of the city’s<br>infrastructure.  They, and similar facilities, are permitted if located<br>under ground. However, overhead lines have the potential to detract<br>from the residential streetscape, and have to be dealt with as<br>discretionary activities. Maintenance and operation of existing utilities<br>is permitted in accordance with the definition of "maintenance" in<br>Chapter 2 (meanings of words).|

|ICr.52.4<br>a)<br>the size and scale of the structures.<br>b)<br>any visual impacts, taking account of the character of the area.<br>c)<br>safety considerations including any effects on line of sight for motorists<br>and other road users, having regard to the usage of the road.|ICr.52.5<br>This rule allows for the usual basic infrastructure in the road reserve at<br>a scale that is generally accepted by the public.  This infrastructure<br>includes street lights and other traffic equipment, as well as electricity<br>distribution boxes and telephone booths.<br>The rule is not restricted to network utility operators in order to<br>regulate bus shelters, street vendors, and the use of the road reserve<br>for pavement cafes.<br>The Council (and the NZ Transport Agency in the case of State<br>Highways) has an additional control as the owner of the land, in<br>respect of who goes there and under what circumstances.<br>Telecommunications and electricity operators have certain rights to<br>put works on roads (under the Telecommunications Act 1987, section<br>15, and Electricity Act 1992, section 24). |ICr.53.4<br>a)<br>the mandatory matters in Chapter 4 of the Nelson Tasman Land<br>Development Manual 2019.<br>b)<br>the noise and air emissions from the road, taking account of the nature of<br>nearby activities.<br>c)<br>any implications for traffic and pedestrian safety, both positive and<br>adverse.<br>d)<br>any proposals to mitigate the adverse effects of the road, particularly by<br>screening for noise and visual impacts.<br>e)<br>any impacts on communities eg. whether the road would divide a<br>neighbourhood.<br>f)<br>any opportunities to provide views and vistas from the road.|ICr.53.5<br>New roads and realignments and upgrading work on existing roads<br>are generally dealt with by way of designations in the Plan. Where new roads have not<br>been dealt with by designation, this rule provides the opportunity for<br>public input via the resource consent process if the road is to be a<br>major traffic carrier, or the usual design standards are not being<br>followed.|
|ICr.54.4<br>a)<br>the ground level required to avoid the effects of anticipated flooding.<br>b)<br>the type of inundation likely to be experienced, whether it be stormwater<br>ponding, tidal inundation, or some other combination of circumstances which<br>could lead to surface flooding.<br>c)<br>the effects on neighbouring properties, especially with respect to<br>stormwater runoff.<br>d)<br>Chapter 5, section 5.4.5 of the Nelson Tasman Land Development<br>Manual 2019.|ICr.54.5<br>The minimum ground levels set are based on the best estimates from<br>the Ministry for the Environment for likely sea level rise caused by<br>global climate change.  This takes account of predicted spring tides<br>and expected tidal surges, and their consequent effects on<br>stormwater ponding.<br>Sites below the minimum levels stated for permitted activities will be<br>assessed individually to ensure that ground or floor heights are<br>sufficient to protect the building from inundation.<br>See Rule ICr.55 (earthworks) where a site is to be filled.<br>Note: This low lying site rule does not apply within the Inundation<br>Overlay - see ICr.59 (inundation overlays)<br>.|

|---|---|---|---|
|**ICr.55**<br>**Earthworks**<br>[note – this rule<br>is a regional and<br>a district rule]|ICr.55.1<br>Earthworks are a permitted activity if:<br>a)<br>the maximum height or depth of excavation or<br>filling does not exceed 1.2m; or<br>b)<br>the earthworks are for the purpose of<br>installation and maintenance of utility service lines<br>including the excavation of holes for supporting<br>structures, back-filled trenches, mole ploughing or<br>thrusting, providing the earthworks are no more than<br>required to permit the activity, or<br>c)    the excavation or fill:<br>i) is retained immediately by a structure authorised<br>by a building consent, and<br>ii) the maximum height or depth of the fill or<br>excavation does not exceed 3m, and<br>iii)  the depth of any excavation adjacent to a<br>property boundary does not exceed the distance<br>from that boundary measured on a horizontal plane,<br>and<br>d)<br>the earthworks do not take place within 10m of<br>the banks of any  river  identified in Appendix 6<br>(riparian and coastal margin overlays), or within 20m<br>of the Coastal Marine Area, except for the purpose<br>of:<br>i)<br>maintaining a State Highway and other roads,<br>or<br>ii)<br>forming or constructing a fire break, fence line,<br>survey line, or<br>iii)<br>installing a utility service line across a river, or<br>iv) is for the purpose of installation and<br>maintenance of utility service lines including the<br>excavation of holes for supporting structures, back-<br>filled trenches, mole ploughing or thrusting, providing<br>the earthworks are no more than required to permit<br>the activity, and<br>e)<br>no soil is positioned where it may dam or divert<br>any river or stream or adversely affect instream<br>habitats, and<br>f)<br>all bare soil areas are, as soon as practicable<br>but no later than six months from the date of<br>disturbance:<br>i) stabilised so that no earth moves off-site or<br>presents a danger to life or property; and<br>ii) vegetated, paved, metalled or built over, and<br>g)<br>after reasonable mixing there is no conspicuous<br>change in the colour or visual clarity in any water<br>body or coastal water as a result of undertaking the<br>activity, and<br>h)<br>all formation surfaces with an inward cross fall<br>are drained by a water table and cut-offs or culverts<br>are formed or installed so as to prevent erosion of<br>the formed surfaces, and<br>i)<br>trenches formed for utility service lines are back<br>filled, compacted and revegetated as soon as<br>practicable, and<br>j)<br>material used for fill is cleanfill material, and<br>k)<br>soil is managed on the site during the<br>construction period and after, such that there are no<br>adverse effects on adjoining properties or any<br>waterbodies.|<br>ICr.55.2<br>Earthworks that contravene a permitted<br>condition are controlled if:<br>a)<br>the maximum height or depth of filling or<br>excavation does not exceed 4m, and<br>b)<br>the site is not in the Land Management<br>Overlay, and<br>c)<br>earthworks do not take place within 10m<br>of the banks of any  river identified in Appendix<br>6 (riparian and coastal margin overlays),  or<br>within 20m of the Coastal Marine Area, and<br>d)<br>no soil is positioned where it may dam or<br>divert any river or stream or adversely affect<br>instream habitats, and<br>e)<br>all bare soil areas are, as soon as<br>practicable but no later than six months from<br>the date of disturbance, or the time specified in<br>the sedimentation and erosion control plan for<br>the site:<br>i)<br>stabilised so that no earth moves off-site<br>or presents a danger to life or property; and<br>ii)<br>vegetated, paved, metalled or built over,<br>and<br>f)<br>all formation surfaces with an inward<br>cross fall are drained by a water table, and cut-<br>offs or culverts  are formed or installed so as to<br>prevent erosion of the formed surfaces, and<br>g)      material used for fill is cleanfill material.<br>Control reserved over:<br>i)<br>loss of topsoil or movement of soil down<br>slope, and<br>ii)<br>damage to structures or adjoining<br>properties, and<br>iii)<br>soil and vegetation entering rivers or<br>coastal water, and<br>iv) damage to instream and coastal habitats,<br>and<br>v)<br>adverse effects on catchment stream<br>flow, including stormwater, and<br>vi) river bank and coastal erosion, and<br>vii) duration of exposure of bare soil to wind<br>and rainfall, and<br>viii) water quality, including suspended<br>sediment load and increased stream bed load,<br>and<br>ix) the method and timing of the activity, and<br>x)<br>the area to be disturbed at any one time,<br>and<br>xi) the provision of structures to control soil<br>erosion or sedimentation, and<br>xii) the timing and techniques used for<br>revegetation, and<br>xiii) the depth, height and volume of cut and<br>fill and the finished ground level, and<br>xiv) the quality of fill material and compaction<br>methods, and<br>xv) visual effects, and<br>xvi) control of noise, and<br>xvii) control of dust, and<br>xviii) traffic and access issues.|ICr.55.3<br>Earthworks that contravene a<br>controlled standard other than g)<br>are restricted discretionary<br>activities.  Where g) is<br>contravened the activity is a<br>discretionary activity.<br>Discretion restricted to:<br>i)<br>loss of topsoil or movement<br>of soil down slope, and<br>ii)<br>the potential for slope failure,<br>and<br>iii)<br>damage to structures or<br>adjoining properties, and<br>iv) soil and vegetation entering<br>rivers and coastal water, and<br>v)<br>damage to instream and<br>coastal habitats, and<br>vi) adverse effects on<br>catchment stream flow, and<br>vii) bank and coastal erosion,<br>and<br>viii) duration of bare soil to wind<br>and rainfall, and<br>ix) water quality, including<br>suspended sediment load and<br>increased stream bed load, and<br>x)<br>the method and timing of the<br>activity, and<br>xi) the area to be cleared at any<br>one time, and<br>xii) the provision of structures to<br>control soil erosion or<br>sedimentation, and<br>xiii) the timing and techniques<br>used for revegetation, and<br>xiv) the long term management<br>of the land cleared, and<br>xv) the provision of appropriate<br>resources to ensure that adverse<br>effects arising from emergency or<br>unforeseen circumstances are<br>controlled or mitigated, and<br>xvi) visual effects, and<br>xvii) the impact on privacy and on<br>the admission of daylight and<br>sunlight to neighbouring sites,<br>and<br>xviii) the values set out in<br>Appendix 6 Table 6.1 for any river,<br>and<br>xix) the matters in Appendix 9<br>(landscape components and<br>views), and<br>xxi)   control of noise, and<br>xxii)   control of dust, and<br>xxiii)   traffic and access issues.|

|**ICr.77**<br>**Access**|ICr.77.1<br>Vehicle access must be provided and<br>maintained on each site in accordance with<br>the standards set out in Appendix 11 (access<br>standards).|<br>ICr.77.2<br>not applicable|ICr.77.3<br>Activities that contravene a permitted condition<br>are discretionary.|

fault areas and slope risk overlays, and whether any risks can be<br>remedied or mitigated.<br>f)<br>the pattern of subdivision and how it relates to the desired environmental outcomes,<br>amenity values for the locality and efficient use of infrastructure.<br>g) the actual and legal protection of significant natural features or heritage items, and<br>means to avoid or mitigate significant changes to the landscape or amenity values of<br>the area.<br>h) the extent to which the proposal has regard to Maori values, particularly any<br>traditional, cultural, or spiritual aspect  relating to the land.<br>i)<br>any consultation, including with Tangata Whenua as appropriate, and the outcome<br>of  that consultation.<br>j)<br>avoidance, remedy or mitigation of adverse effects of the subdivision, including<br>temporary effects of construction.<br>k)<br>financial contributions (see Chapter 6).<br>l)<br>the development potential of other adjacent land.<br>m) the ground level required to avoid the effects of flooding.<br>n) the type of inundation likely to be experienced, whether it be stormwater ponding,<br>tidal inundation, or some other combination of circumstances which could lead to<br>surface flooding.<br>o)<br>effects on neighbouring properties, especially stormwater runoff.<br>p)<br>provision of adequate flow paths for surface flooding.<br>q) the possibility of an overloaded public storm water system overflowing onto private<br>property.<br>r)<br>effects of allotment size and shape, including on amenities of neighbourhood and on<br>the potential efficiency and range of uses of the land.<br>s) the values for esplanade purposes outlined in Table 6.1 or 6.2, Appendix 6, including<br>any additional information regarding the values of the reserve or strip sought for the<br>purposes outlined in section 229 of the Act.<br>t)<br>any circumstances which make the taking of the esplanade reserve or strip (or the<br>width stated in Appendix 6, Table 6.2) inappropriate, including (but not limited to) the<br>nature of existing development, reasons of security, public safety, minor boundary<br>adjustment.<br>u) an existing protection of the area including any existing esplanade reserves or strips<br>or any protective covenants.<br>v) alternative ways in which the esplanade values identified  in the area can be<br>provided for including (but not limited to ) the use of esplanade strips and protective<br>covenants.<br>w) the assessment matters in Table DO6.1.1 regarding the type of protection<br>appropriate in given circumstances.|

|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|

|SCr.26.4<br>a)<br>the effects on the amenity of neighbouring properties.<br>b)<br>any provision for compensating landscaping or screening.<br>c)<br>the scale and height of the buildings within the reduced setback.<br>d)<br>the ability to better use the site and provide better environmental<br>quality elsewhere on the site.<br>e)<br>any aspects of the proposal which may compensate for<br>reduced landscaping or screening, such as the nature of<br>planting or materials used, the location of parking, manoeuvring<br>or storage areas, and offices.|<br> <br>SCr.26.5<br>This provision ensures a degree of outlook is maintained<br>from residential properties, and provides opportunity to soften<br>that outlook by planting or other site treatments.<br>Landscaping along the zone boundary can be to an average<br>depth, to provide for variability in depth, thus increasing visual<br>interest.<br>Buildings that form part of a telecommunications service (as<br>defined by the Telecommunications Act 2001 or relevant<br>amendments) are permitted to be located within these<br>setbacks because they are considered to have no more than<br>minor visual effects in this semi-commercial environment,<br>especially as compared to other residential buildings which<br>are permitted as of right to be located closer to a boundary.<br>An important difference between the telecommunications<br>network and some other network utilities is that<br>telecommunications networks do not include such facilities as<br>substations, which for other reasons may be considered to be<br>unacceptable in the residential environment.<br>Note that all structures and buildings must still comply with<br>rule SCr27 “Daylight Admission” which protects neighbouring<br>properties from the shading effects of buildings located very<br>close to their boundaries.|
|SCr.27.4<br>a)<br>the effects of any shading on the public enjoyment and amenity<br>of residential areas.<br>b)<br>the extent of any additional shading, having regard to the size of<br>the shadow cast and the period of time any area is affected by it<br>(eg. tall thin shadow compared to shorter, bulky shadow taking<br>longer to pass).<br>c)<br>the nature of the activities undertaken in any area affected.|<br> <br>SCr.27.5<br>The sunlight and daylight controls are set so that a<br>residentially zoned property is not penalised having a<br>commercial rather than a residential neighbour.|



**Nelson Resource Management Plan (26/01/08)** **9-17**


|Item|Permitted|Controlled|Discretionary/Non-<br>complying|
|---|---|---|---|
|**SCr.28**<br>**Building over or**<br>**alongside drains**<br>**(piped or open)**<br>**and water mains**|SCr.28.1<br>Structures 3metres or greater from a drain<br>(piped or open) are a permitted activity.<br>Structures closer than 3metres to a piped<br>drain or watermain are permitted provided<br>that:<br>For drains or watermains less than or equal<br>to 300mm diameter:<br>a) any structure must be located no closer<br>than 1metre measured horizontally from<br>the near side of any public unsleeved<br>water main or common private or public<br>sewer or stormwater drain, or<br>For drains or watermains greater than<br>300mm in diameter<br>b) any structure must be located no closer<br>than 1.5metre measured horizontally from<br>the near side of any public water main, or<br>common private or public sewer or<br>stormwater drain, or<br>For drains 150mm or less in diameter<br>c) any structure may be located within<br>1metre or directly over a common private<br>or public drain if the diameter of the pipe<br>is 150mm or less; providing that:<br>i) The length of pipe or drain built over<br>is no more than 6 meters in length;<br>and<br>ii) There are no changes in direction or<br>junctions in the portion of the drain<br>built over; and<br>iii) The length of drain built over is<br>relaid using a continuouslengthof<br>pipe without joints,sleevedinside a<br>225mm diameter class 4 concrete<br>pipe; and<br>iv) There is a minimum 6metre clear<br>length and 3metre clear width and<br>1.8metre clear height at one end of<br>the sleeve to allow replacement of the<br>pipe; and<br>v) The pipes are not water mains or<br>pressurised pipelines;<br>and in all cases<br>d) any structure may overhang the line of<br>the pipe or drain, provided the structure is<br>cantilevered or is an eave and the height<br>to the underside of the structure above<br>ground level is not less than 1.8metres<br>where the required pipe or drain is<br>greater than 150mm in diameter or width;<br>and<br>e) any structure located within 3metres,<br>measured horizontally, from the near side<br>of the pipe or drain must have the base of<br>the foundations deeper than a line drawn<br>at 30 degrees from the horizontal from<br>the invert (bottom) of the pipe or drain (or<br>between 30 degrees and 45 degrees if<br>the design has been certified by a<br>suitably qualified engineer)(see diagram).|<br> <br> <br> <br> <br>SCr.28.2<br>Structures:<br>That contravene c) ii) to vi) only<br>are controlled activities<br>The matters of control are;<br>a) Physical accessibility to the<br>pipe, and<br>b) The ground/floor type and<br>design used to provide quick<br>and easy removal to provide<br>the ability to access the pipes<br>for maintenance and repair,<br>and<br>c) The depth of<br>concrete/permanent surface<br>floor over the pipe, and<br>d) Alternative locations for the<br>pipe and methods of<br>emplacement.|SCr.28.3<br>Buildings, swimming<br>pools or fences within<br>3m of the top of bank of<br>an open drain is a<br>discretionary activity.<br>All other activities are<br>discretionary.|

**9-24** **(30/04/12) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|

|SCr.43.4<br>a) the potential effects of any increase of radiofrequency<br>exposures on the health of persons near the facility.<br>b) the nature of any activities near the proposed site, having<br>regard to their susceptibility to any exposures.<br>c)<br>the location of the site, and any potential for shielding from<br>exposures.<br>d) any cumulative effects, particularly with regard to exposure to<br>electromagnetic radiation from existing facilities in the area.|SCr.43.5<br>Certain utilities and other activities emit electromagnetic<br>radiation. These activities are perceived to be a health concern to<br>some people living near them.<br>In developing the rules on radiofrequency exposures, Council<br>has based its approach on that recommended in the “National<br>Guidelines for Managing the Effects of Radiofrequency<br>Transmitters” produced by the Ministry of Health and the Ministry<br>for the Environment in December 2000.  The key findings of the<br>guidelines was that there are no established health effects from<br>exposure to radiofrequency fields as long as they comply with<br>the New Zealand Standard NZS 2772.1:1999 Radiofrequency<br>Fields: Part 1 – Maximum Exposure Levels 3kHz-300GHz.<br>The Council is to be notified of location and nature of any<br>proposed facility.  Should this predictive report anticipate and<br>should exposure levels be greater than 25% of the New Zealand<br>Standard level, monitoring to determine the actual exposure<br>levels from the transmitting installation will be required.<br>The rule contains an exception for domestic radiofrequency<br>transmitting equipment.  This is to ensure that these domestic<br>transmitting devices can be used without the rules applying to<br>their radiofrequency emissions.<br>Radiofrequency emissions that exceed the exposure levels set<br>within the New Zealand Standard are to be considered as non-<br>complying activities.|
|SCr.44.4<br>a)<br>any hazard presented by the utility.<br>b)<br>the environmental setting of the structure, having regard to<br>the general locality, topography, geographical features and<br>adjacent land uses.<br>c)<br>the visual impacts of the structure on residential or<br>recreational use of  land in the vicinity, and on significant<br>ridge lines and view planes from public places, including<br>roads.<br>d)<br>the scale, bulk and height of the facility.<br>e)<br>screening or landscaping of the utility and any modifications<br>to its colour and design to reduce the visual effect of the<br>utility on the surrounding environment.<br>f)<br>any constraints on placing the utility underground.|SCr.44.5<br>Provision is made for lower pressure gas lines as permitted<br>activities, but high pressure lines which present a higher risk<br>need to be assessed as discretionary activities.<br>The electricity and telephone network is an important part of the<br>city’s infrastructure.  They, and similar facilities, are permitted if<br>located under ground. However, overhead lines have the<br>potential to detract from the streetscape, and have to be dealt<br>with as discretionary activities. Maintenance and operation of<br>existing utilities is permitted in accordance with the definition of<br>"maintenance" in Chapter 2 Meaning of Words.|

|SCr.45.4<br>a)<br>the size and scale of the structures.<br>b)<br>any visual impacts, taking account of the character of the<br>area.<br>c)<br>safety considerations including any effects on line of sight<br>for motorists and other road users, having regard to the<br>usage of the road.|SCr.45.5<br>This rule allows for the usual basic infrastructure in the road<br>reserve at a scale that is generally accepted by the public. The Council will<br>be guided when it prescribes conditions under these Acts, by the<br>matters contemplated in these rules.|
|SCr.46.4<br>a)<br>the matters in the Nelson Tasman Land Development<br>Manual 2019.<br>b)<br>the noise and air emissions from the road, taking account<br>of the nature of nearby activities.<br>c)<br>any implications for traffic and pedestrian safety, both<br>positive and adverse.<br>d)<br>any proposals to mitigate the adverse effects of the road,<br>particularly by screening for noise and visual impacts.<br>e)<br>any impacts on communities eg. whether the road would<br>divide a neighbourhood.<br>f)<br>any opportunities to provide views and vistas from the<br>road.|SCr.46.5<br>New roads and realignments and upgrading work on existing<br>roads are generally dealt with by way of designations in the Plan.<br>The designation procedure provides an opportunity for the public<br>or affected persons to have a say on the proposals and for the<br>environmental effects to be scrutinised.  Where new roads have<br>not been dealt with by designation, this rule provides the<br>opportunity for public input via the resource consent process if the<br>road is to be a major traffic carrier, or the usual design standards<br>are not being followed.|
|SCr.47.4<br>a)<br>the ground level required to avoid the effects of anticipated<br>flooding.<br>b)<br>the type of inundation likely to be experienced, whether it<br>be stormwater ponding, tidal inundation, or some other<br>combination of circumstances which could lead to surface<br>flooding.<br>c)<br>the effects on neighbouring properties, especially with<br>respect to stormwater runoff.<br>d)<br>the matters in section 4 of the Nelson Tasman Land<br>Development Manual 2019.|SCr.47.5<br>The minimum ground levels set are based on the best estimates<br>from the Ministry for the Environment for likely sea level rise<br>caused by global climate change.  This takes account of predicted<br>spring tides and expected tidal surges, and their consequent<br>effects on stormwater ponding.<br>Sites below the minimum levels stated for permitted activities will<br>be assessed individually to ensure that ground or floor heights are<br>sufficient to protect the building from inundation.<br>See Rule SCr.48 (earthworks) where a site is to be filled.<br>This low lying site rule does not apply within the Inundation<br>Overlay.|



**Nelson Resource Management Plan (12/07/21)** **9-35**


|Item|Permitted|Controlled|Discretionary/Non-complying|
|---|---|---|---|
|**SCr.48**<br>**Earthworks**<br>[Note that this is<br>a regional and a<br>district rule]|SCr.48.1<br>Earthworks are a permitted activity if:<br>a)  the maximum height or depth of excavation or<br>filling does not exceed 1.2m, or<br>b) the earthworks are for the purpose of installation<br>and maintenance of utility service lines including<br>the excavation of holes for supporting structures,<br>back-filled trenches, mole ploughing or thrusting,<br>providing the earthworks are no more than<br>required to permit the activity, or<br>c) the excavation or fill:<br>i)  is retained immediately by a structure authorised<br>by a building consent, and<br>ii)  the maximum height or depth of the fill does not<br>exceed 3m, and<br>iii)  the depth of any excavation adjacent to a<br>property boundary does not exceed the distance<br>from that boundary measured on a horizontal<br>plane, and<br>d) the earthworks do not take place within 10m of the<br>banks of any river identified in Appendix 6 (riparian<br>and coastal margin overlays), or within 20m of the<br>Coastal Marine Area, except for the purpose of:<br>i) maintaining a state highway and other roads, or<br>ii) forming or constructing a fire break, fence line,<br>survey line, or<br>iii) installing a utility service line across a river, or<br>iv) is for the purpose of installation and maintenance<br>of utility service lines including the excavation of<br>holes for supporting structures, back-filled<br>trenches,  mole ploughing or thrusting, providing<br>the earthworks are no more than required to<br>permit the activity; and<br>e) no soil is positioned where it may dam or divert any<br>river or stream or adversely effect instream habitats,<br>and<br>f)  all bare soil areas are, as soon as practicable but no<br>later than six months from the date of disturbance:<br>i) stabilised so that no earth moves off-site or<br>presents a danger to life or property; and<br>ii) vegetated, paved, metalled or built over, and<br>g) after reasonable mixing there is no conspicuous<br>change in the colour or visual clarity in any water<br>body or coastal water as a result of undertaking the<br>activity, and<br>h)    all formation surfaces with an inward cross fall are<br>drained by a water table and cut-offs or culverts are<br>formed or installed so as to prevent erosion of the<br>formed surfaces, and<br>i) trenches formed for utility service lines are back<br>filled, compacted and revegetated as soon as<br>practicable, and<br>j) material used for fill is cleanfill material, and<br>k)  soil is managed on the site during the construction<br>period and after, such that there are no adverse<br>effects on adjoining properties or any waterbodies.|<br>SCr.48.2<br>Earthworks that contravene a permitted<br>condition are controlled if:<br>a) the maximum height or depth of filling<br>or excavation does not exceed 4m,<br>and<br>b) the site is not in the Land Management<br>Overlay, and<br>c) earthworks do not take place within<br>10m of the banks of any river shown in<br>the Riparian Overlay on the Planning<br>Maps and contained in Appendix 6; or<br>within20 m of the Coastal Marine Area,<br>and<br>d) no soil is positioned where it may dam<br>or divert any river or stream or<br>adversely affect instream habitats, and<br>e) all bare soil areas are, as soon as<br>practicable but no later than six months<br>from the date of disturbance, or the<br>time specified in the sedimentation and<br>erosion control plan for the site:<br>i) stabilised so that no earth moves off-<br>site or presents a danger to life or<br>property; and<br>ii) vegetated, paved, metalled or built<br>over, and<br>f) all formation surfaces with an inward<br>cross fall are drained by a water table,<br>and cut-offs or culverts are formed or<br>installed so as to prevent erosion of the<br>formed surfaces, and<br>g)     material used for fill is cleanfill<br>material.<br>Control reserved over:<br>i) loss of topsoil or movement of soil<br>down slope, and<br>ii) damage to structures or adjoining<br>properties, and<br>iii) soil and vegetation entering rivers or<br>coastal water, and<br>iv) damage to instream and coastal<br>habitats, and<br>v) adverse effects on catchment stream<br>flow, including stormwater, and<br>vi) river bank and coastal erosion, and<br>vii) duration of exposure of bare soil to<br>wind and rainfall, and<br>viii) water quality, including suspended<br>sediment load and increased stream<br>bed load, and<br>ix) the method and timing of the activity,<br>and<br>x) the area to be disturbed at any one<br>time, and<br>xi) the provision of structures to control<br>soil erosion or sedimentation, and<br>xii) the timing and techniques used for<br>revegetation, and<br>xiii) the depth, height and volume of cut<br>and fill and the finished ground level,<br>and<br>xiv) the quality of fill material and<br>compaction methods, and<br>xv) visual effects, and<br>xvi)  control of noise, and<br>xvii)  control of dust, and<br>xviii) traffic and access issues.|<br>SCr.48.3<br>Earthworks that contravene a<br>controlled standard other than g) are<br>restricted discretionary activities.<br>Where g) is contravened the activity is a<br>discretionary activity.<br>Discretion restricted to:<br>i) loss of topsoil or movement of soil<br>down slope, and<br>ii) the potential for slope failure, and<br>iii) damage to structures or adjoining<br>properties, and<br>iv) soil and vegetation entering rivers<br>and coastal water, and<br>v) damage to instream and coastal<br>habitats, and<br>vi) adverse effects on catchment<br>stream flow, and<br>vii) bank and coastal erosion, and<br>viii) duration of bare soil to wind and<br>rainfall, and<br>ix) water quality, including suspended<br>sediment load and increased<br>stream bed load, and<br>x) the method and timing of the<br>activity, and<br>xi) the area to be cleared at any one<br>time, and<br>xii) the provision of structures to control<br>soil erosion or sedimentation, and<br>xiii) the timing and techniques used for<br>revegetation, and<br>xiv) the long term management of the<br>land cleared, and<br>xv) the provision of appropriate<br>resources to ensure that adverse<br>effects arising from emergency or<br>unforeseen circumstances are<br>controlled or mitigated, and<br>xvi) visual effects, and<br>xvii) the impacts on privacy and on the<br>admission of daylight and sunlight<br>to neighbouring sites, and<br>xviii) in the case of earthworks within<br>the Landscape Overlays,<br>compliance with the objectives and<br>performance guidelines in Appendix<br>6 (Guide for Subdivision in<br>Landscape Overlays), **9-36** **(12/11/12) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|SCr.57.4<br>a)<br>the effect of the proposed new building on the integrity of<br>the original heritage building or object, taking account of<br>how visible the change will be.<br>b)<br>the degree to which the new building is compatible with<br>the heritage building or object, including size, scale and<br>materials used.<br>c)<br>the location of the new building in relation to the heritage<br>building or object and whether it dominates or detracts<br>from the heritage building or object.|SCr.57.5<br>This rule ensures that new buildings on the site of an existing<br>heritage building, place or object are compatible with the existing<br>heritage item.  Distance from the heritage item is an important<br>consideration, particularly where the proposed new building is in<br>very close proximity to the heritage item.  See separate rules for<br>Heritage Precincts.|
|SCr.58.4<br>a)<br>the historic, cultural or architectural significance of the item,<br>having regard to the site on which the item is located.<br>b)<br>the extent to which the building has particular value because<br>of the scarcity of heritage buildings in the area, or because it<br>forms part of a precinct of heritage buildings.<br>c)<br>for removal, the degree of heritage loss due to the<br>association of the building with the present site and the<br>physical extent of relocation.<br>d)<br>the location a building or object is to be moved to, having<br>regard to whether this yields a net environmental gain (eg.<br>the new site is more accessible or visible), and whether the<br>item is to be protected or covenanted on its new site.<br>e)<br>whether part of the building, place or object can be kept,<br>while still maintaining to a reasonable degree, the features<br>for which the item was listed.<br>f)<br>the ability of the applicant to economically develop or use<br>the site without demolition, alteration or removal.<br>g)<br>the nature of any activity that is proposed to occur on the<br>site, including the design and appearance of any<br>replacement building or object.  (The degree of compliance<br>with the Design Guide for the Russell Street Heritage<br>Precinct where relevant).<br>h)<br>whether the heritage value of the building, place or object<br>has altered since the item was listed in the Plan.<br>i)<br>any immediate or cumulative effects of the loss or removal<br>of the listed building, place or object on the range, number,<br>and quality of heritage features in the vicinity and the city as<br>a whole.|<br>SCr.58.5<br>Group A buildings, places and objects are the premier heritage<br>items in the District.  Their removal or demolition therefore is a<br>non-complying activity under the Plan.  A lower threshold can be<br>applied to Group B items, while recognising that their retention is<br>still important.<br>Buildings and objects may have different strengths of association<br>with their site and situation.  Relocation on the same site or to an<br>adjoining site may have limited adverse effects, while relocation<br>to a site further away may have a greater adverse effect.|
|SCr.59.4<br>a)<br>whether reducing the notification time would disadvantage<br>any party, or would preclude effort to negotiate retention of<br>the item.|SCr.59.5<br>The requirement for 2 months notice for Group C items allows<br>time for photographic or other records to be made of the heritage<br>building or item prior to it being demolished (the Council will<br>maintain such records and archival material).  It also provides the<br>opportunity for interested parties to negotiate voluntary protection<br>of the heritage item.  This might include purchase or some other<br>arrangement to the satisfaction of the property owner.|

**9- 46                                      (12/07/21) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|SCr.60.4<br>a)<br>particular regard will be had to compliance with the<br>Design Guide for the Russell St Heritage Precinct where<br>relevant.<br>b)<br>In addition regard will be had to:<br>i) any effects (positive and adverse) on the heritage<br>values of the entire heritage precinct.<br>ii) any cumulative or precedent effects on the heritage<br>values of the precinct.|<br>SCr.60.5<br>The heritage precincts recognise the whole is often greater than the<br>sum of the parts.  That is, that a collection of heritage buildings in<br>context, has a greater impact to the observer and the resident, and<br>has greater heritage value, than the same number of buildings<br>scattered throughout the City.<br>Unsympathetic alteration to even a single heritage building can have<br>major impacts on the entire precinct. The controls therefore focus on<br>ensuring that any significant alterations to buildings are in keeping<br>with the heritage values of the precinct.<br>The design controls include existing non-listed buildings within the<br>heritage precinct.  The purpose of this is to promote a gradual<br>improvement in the compatibility of these buildings with the heritage<br>buildings, where this is practicable.<br>The design criteria to achieve development sympathetic to each<br>precinct are spelt out in the design guideline for that precinct (see<br>section AD10.2 – documents related to this plan).  The guidelines sit<br>outside the Plan, but are given effect as assessment criteria in<br>considering consent applications.  These consents are restricted<br>discretionary activities, in order to provide flexibility to control matters<br>such as building height, and site area which can vary between<br>precincts, and where the normal rules may not be appropriate.<br>See also Ap20r.4 in relation to signs on heritage buildings and trees.|

**9-58** **(12/07/21) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


**suburban commercial zone**






|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|SCr.71.4<br>a)<br>the matters in the Nelson Tasman Land Development Manual<br>2019.<br>b)        the extent of compliance with any plan provisions relating to<br>streams, drains leading to streams, and any other waterbodies<br>on the land to be subdivided, and<br>c)<br>the extent of compliance with Appendices 10 to 12, and<br>d)<br>effects on traffic, road network, access, parking, stormwater<br>management, water supply, sewage reticulation, and power<br>and telecommunication services.<br>e)<br>the extent to which the land is subject to natural hazards, or<br>included in inundation, floodpaths, fault areas and slope risk<br>overlays, and whether any risks can be remedied or mitigated.<br>f)<br>the pattern of subdivision and how it relates to the desired<br>environmental outcomes, amenity values for the locality, and<br>efficient use of infrastructure.<br>g)<br>the actual and legal protection of significant natural features or<br>heritage items, and means to avoid or mitigate significant<br>changes to the landscape or amenity values of the area.<br>h)<br>the extent to which the proposal has regard to Maori values,<br>particularly any consultation.<br>j)<br>avoidance, remedy or mitigation of adverse effects of the<br>subdivision, including temporary effects of construction.<br>k)<br>financial contributions (see Chapter 6).<br>l)<br>the development potential of other adjacent land.<br>m)<br>the ground level required to avoid the effects of flooding.<br>n)<br>the type of inundation likely to be experienced, whether it be<br>stormwater ponding, tidal inundation, or some other<br>combination of circumstances which could lead to surface<br>flooding.<br>o)<br>effects on neighbouring properties, especially stormwater runoff.<br>p)<br>provision of adequate flow paths for surface flooding.<br>q)<br>the possibility of an overloaded public storm water system<br>overflowing onto private property.<br>r)<br>effects of allotment size and shape, including on amenities of<br>the neighbourhood and on the potential efficiency and range of<br>uses of the land.<br>s)<br>the values for esplanade purposes outlined in Table 6.1 or 6.2,<br>Appendix 6 (riparian and coastal margin overlays), including<br>any additional information regarding the values of the reserve or<br>strip sought for the purposes outlined in section 229 of the Act.<br>t)<br>any circumstances which make the taking of the esplanade<br>reserve or strip (or the width stated in Appendix 6, Table 6.2)<br>inappropriate, including (but not limited to) the nature of existing<br>development, reasons of security, public safety, minor boundary<br>adjustment.<br>u)<br>an existing protection of the area including any existing<br>esplanade reserves or strips or any protective covenants.<br>v)<br>alternative ways in which the esplanade values identified  in the<br>area can be provided for including (but not limited to ) the use of<br>esplanade strips and protective covenants).<br>w)<br>the assessment matters in Table DO6.1.1 regarding the type of<br>protection appropriate ingiven circumstances.|<br> <br>SCr.71.5<br>Specific rules apply to subdivision activities proposed within<br>the Heritage Overlay or Heritage Precinct (see Rule SCr.72<br>and SCr73).<br>Subdivision is a controlled activity so that conditions can be<br>imposed on the development to ensure a satisfactory<br>standard of amenity, the minimisation of adverse effects and<br>that the site can be adequately serviced.<br>There is no minimum size for allotments, leaving this to the<br>market to determine.  Subdividers should note that the<br>proposed allotment should be capable of accommodating a<br>building or an activity which complies with the rules in this<br>Zone.<br>The controls also enable consideration to be had to the<br>development potential of nearby land, so that the level of<br>servicing provided is appropriate to the likely future demand in<br>the area.  This allows consideration of future roading patterns,<br>and demands on sewers and other services, to avoid the<br>need for costly and disruptive upgrading later.<br>The Act states the preservation of the natural character of the<br>river and coastal margins to be matters of national<br>importance.  This includes public access along these, and<br>protection of areas of significant indigenous flora and the<br>habitats of indigenous fauna, contained within them. It<br>provides a number of mechanisms to achieve this protection<br>including the taking of esplanade reserves and strips.<br>The river and coastal margins on the Planning Maps and in<br>Appendix 6, Table 6.2 (riparian or coastal areas with priority<br>values), have been identified as containing riparian values in<br>accord with section 229 of the Act. In some cases riparian<br>protection already exists, or special circumstances exist,<br>which make the taking of esplanade reserves or strips<br>unnecessary.  In other cases a lesser width, or an alternative<br>way of achieving riparian protection may be more<br>appropriate.  In these situations, a discretionary consent<br>application is needed, in order to depart from the standards<br>set out for a normal subdivision.<br>Where a subdivision is discretionary, and the allotment<br>adjoins any river or the coastal margin, then an esplanade<br>reserve or strip may be required as a condition of the<br>subdivision consent, having regard to the values identified in<br>Appendix 6, Table 6.1 (riparian and coastal margins with<br>identified riparian values).<br>The minimum ground levels set are based on the best<br>estimates from the Ministry for the Environment for likely sea<br>level rise caused by global climate change.  This takes<br>account of predicted spring tides and expected tidal surges,<br>and their consequent effects on stormwater ponding.<br>Sites below the minimum levels stated for controlled activities<br>will be assessed individually to ensure that ground or floor<br>heights are sufficient to protect the site from inundation.<br>See Rule SCr.48 (earthworks) where a site is being filled.|

|**INr.32**<br>**Building over or**<br>**alongside drains and**<br>**water mains**|INr.32.1<br>Structures 3metres or greater from a drain<br>(piped or open) are a permitted activity.<br>Structures closer than 3metres to a piped<br>drain or watermain are permitted provided<br>that:<br>For drains or watermains less than or equal<br>to 300mm diameter:<br>a) any structure must be located no closer<br>than 1metre measured horizontally from<br>the near side of any public unsleeved<br>water main or common private or public<br>sewer or stormwater drain, or<br>For drains or watermains greater than<br>300mm in diameter<br>b) any structure must be located no closer<br>than 1.5metre measured horizontally from<br>the near side of any public water main, or<br>common private or public sewer or<br>stormwater drain, or<br>For drains 150mm or less in diameter<br>c) any structure may be located within 1metre<br>or directly over a common private or public<br>drain if the diameter of the pipe is 150mm<br>or less; providing that:<br>i) The length of pipe or drain built over<br>is no more than 6 meters in length;<br>and<br>ii) There are no changes in direction or<br>junctions in the portion of the drain<br>built over; and<br>iii) The length of drain built over is relaid<br>using a continuouslengthof pipe<br>without joints,sleevedinside a<br>225mm diameter class 4 concrete<br>pipe; and<br>iv) There is a minimum 6metre clear<br>length and 3metre clear width and<br>1.8metre clear height at one end of the<br>sleeve to allow replacement of the<br>pipe; and<br>v) The pipes are not water mains or<br>pressurised pipelines;<br>and in all cases<br>d) any structure may overhang the line of the<br>pipe or drain, provided the structure is<br>cantilevered or is an eave and the height<br>to the underside of the structure above<br>ground level is not less than 1.8metres<br>where the required pipe or drain is greater<br>than 150mm in diameter or width; and<br>e) any structure located within 3metres,<br>measured horizontally, from the near side<br>of the pipe or drain must have the base of<br>the foundations deeper than a line drawn<br>at 30 degrees from the horizontal from the<br>invert (bottom) of the pipe or drain (or<br>between 30 degrees and 45 degrees if the<br>design has been certified by a suitably<br>qualified engineer)(see diagram).|<br>INr.32.2<br>Structures:<br>That contravene c) ii) to vi) only<br>are controlled activities<br>The matters of control are;<br>a) Physical accessibility to the<br>pipe, and<br>b) The ground/floor type and<br>design used to provide quick<br>and easy removal to provide<br>the ability to access the<br>pipes for maintenance and<br>repair, and<br>c) The depth of<br>concrete/permanent surface<br>floor over the pipe, and<br>d) Alternative locations for the<br>pipe and methods of<br>emplacement.|INr.32.3<br>Buildings, swimming pools or<br>fences within 3m of the top of<br>bank of an open drain is a<br>discretionary activity.<br>All other activities are<br>discretionary.<br>.|

For the purposes of<br>this rule, the noise limit to be applied at or<br>within the boundary of Auckland Point School<br>in respect to noise from the Port Operational<br>Area shall be 55 dBA Leq(15 min) between<br>8.30am to 3.30pm Monday to Friday<br>excluding school holidays for as long as the<br>noise limit continues to apply. In the event the<br>above noise levels are exceeded then the<br>classrooms shall be upgraded where<br>necessary to achieve a level of 40 dBA Leq(15<br>min, 8.30am-3.30pm) inside from noise from the Port<br>Operational Area with ventilating windows<br>open. Where windows must be closed to<br>achieve 40 dBA Leq(15 min, 8.30am-3.30pm) an<br>alternative ventilation system shall be<br>provided.|<br> <br> <br>INr.38.2<br>not applicable|INr.38.3<br>Activities which contravene a permitted<br>condition are non-complying.|

|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|

|INr.48.4<br>a) the potential effects of any increase of radiofrequency exposures on the<br>health of persons near the facility.<br>b) the nature of any activities near the proposed site, having regard to their<br>susceptibility to any exposures.<br>c) the location of the site, and any potential for shielding from exposures.<br>d) any cumulative effects, particularly with regard to exposure to<br>electromagnetic radiation from existing facilities in the area.|INr.48.5<br>Certain utilities and other activities emit electromagnetic radiation.<br>These activities are perceived to be a health concern to some people<br>living near them.<br>In developing the rules on radiofrequency exposures, Council has<br>based its approach on that recommended in the “National Guidelines<br>for Managing the Effects of Radiofrequency Transmitters” produced<br>by the Ministry of Health and the Ministry for the Environment in<br>December 2000.  The key findings of the guidelines was that there<br>are no established health effects from exposure to radiofrequency<br>fields as long as they comply with the New Zealand Standard NZS<br>2772.1:1999 Radiofrequency Fields: Part 1 – Maximum Exposure<br>Levels 3kHz-300GHz.<br>The Council is to be notified of location and nature of any proposed<br>facility.  Should this predictive report anticipate and should exposure<br>levels be greater than 25% of the New Zealand Standard level,<br>monitoring to determine the actual exposure levels from the<br>transmitting installation will be required.<br>The rule contains an exception for domestic radiofrequency<br>transmitting equipment.  This is to ensure that these domestic<br>transmitting devices can be used without the rules applying to their<br>radiofrequency emissions.<br>Radiofrequency emissions that exceed the exposure levels set within<br>the New Zealand Standard are to be considered as non-complying<br>activities.|
|INr.49.4<br>a) any hazard presented by the utility.<br>b) the environmental setting of the structure, having regard to the general<br>locality, topography, geographical features and adjacent land uses.<br>c) the visual impacts of the structure on residential or recreational use of<br>land in the vicinity, and on significant ridge lines and view planes from<br>public places, including roads.<br>d) the scale, bulk and height of the facility.<br>e) screening or landscaping of the utility and any modifications to its colour<br>and design to reduce the visual effect of the utility on the surrounding<br>environment.<br>f)<br>any constraints on placing the utility underground.|INr.49.5<br>Provision is made for lower pressure gas lines as permitted activities,<br>but high pressure lines which present a higher risk need to be<br>assessed as discretionary activities.<br>The electricity and telephone network is an important part of the city’s<br>infrastructure.  They, and similar facilities, are permitted if located<br>under ground. However, overhead lines have the potential to detract<br>from the residential streetscape, and have to be dealt with as<br>discretionary activities.   Maintenance and operation of existing<br>utilities is permitted in accordance with the definition of "maintenance"<br>in Chapter 2.|

|**INr.53**<br>**Building on low lying**<br>**sites**|INr.53.1<br>Building is permitted if:<br>a) the ground level (excluding  water<br>bodies) is 15.35m NCC Datum or<br>above; or ground level is raised and<br>compacted  to at least those levels:<br>i) in accordance with NZS 4431:1989<br>(Code of Practice for Earthfill for<br>Residential Development), and<br>ii) such that stormwater runoff from the<br>site is not directed onto other sites or<br>into any river or stream, and natural<br>water flows from other sites are not<br>obstructed, and<br>iii)   the finished ground level is not less<br>than 400mm above the design<br>hydraulic grade level of the storm<br>water system serving the site, and<br>b) the minimum finished floor level of<br>the building is:<br>i) concrete floor: 15.50m<br>ii) timber floor: 15.65m<br>This rule does not apply to ground<br>levels below 15.35m NCC Datum<br>within the Port Operational Area where<br>the appropriate level for a building must<br>be determined by a registered<br>engineer.<br>This rule does not apply to bunded<br>hazardous substance storage areas<br>where the bunding and stormwater<br>system provides inundation protection<br>for that area to a level at or above that<br>specified in this rule.|<br> <br>INr.53.2<br>not applicable|INr.53.3<br>Buildings that contravene a<br>permitted condition are restricted<br>discretionary activities.<br>Discretion is restricted to measures<br>required for the avoidance or<br>mitigation of inundation hazards on<br>the subject and surrounding<br>properties.|

|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|

|INr.53.4<br>a) the ground level required to avoid the effects of anticipated flooding.<br>b) the type of inundation likely to be experienced, whether it be stormwater<br>ponding, tidal inundation, or some other combination of circumstances<br>which could lead to surface flooding.<br>c) the effects on neighbouring properties, especially with respect to<br>stormwater runoff.<br>d) section 5.3.5 of the Nelson Tasman Land Development Manual (2019).|INr.53.5<br>The minimum ground levels set are based on the best estimates<br>from the Ministry for the Environment for likely sea level rise caused<br>by global climate change.  This takes account of predicted spring<br>tides and expected tidal surges, and their consequent effects on<br>stormwater ponding.<br>Sites below the minimum levels stated for permitted activities will be<br>assessed individually to ensure that ground or floor heights are<br>sufficient to protect the building from inundation.<br>See Rule INr.54 (earthworks) where a site is to be filled.<br>Within the Port Operational area a number of transit storage sheds<br>for in transit goods exist. **Nelson Resource Management Plan (12/07/21)** **10-43**


|Item|Permitted|Controlled|Discretionary/Non-complying|
|---|---|---|---|
|**INr.54**<br>**Earthworks**<br>[note – this<br>rule is a<br>regional and<br>a district rule]|INr.54.1<br>Earthworks are a permitted activity if:<br>a) the maximum height or depth of excavation or<br>filling does not exceed 1.2m, or<br>b) the earthworks are for the purpose of installation<br>and maintenance of utility service lines including<br>the excavation of holes for supporting structures,<br>back-filled trenches,  mole ploughing or thrusting,<br>providing the earthworks are no more than<br>required to permit the activity, or<br>c) the excavation or fill:<br>i) is retained immediately by a structure<br>authorised by a building consent, and<br>ii) the maximum height or depth of the fill or<br>excavation does not exceed 3m, and<br>iii)  the depth of any excavation adjacent to a<br>property boundary does not exceed the distance<br>from that boundary measured on a horizontal<br>plane; and<br>d) the earthworks do not take place within 10m of<br>the banks of any river identified in Appendix 6<br>(riparian and coastal margin overlays), or within<br>20m of the Coastal Marine Area, except within<br>the Port Operational Area for the purpose of<br>i) maintaining a State Highway and other roads,<br>forming or constructing a fire break, fence line,<br>survey line or<br>ii) installing a utility service line across a river, or<br>iii) is for the purpose of installation and<br>maintenance of utility service lines including<br>the excavation of holes for supporting<br>structures, back-filled trenches, mole<br>ploughing or thrusting, providing the<br>earthworks are no more than required to<br>permit the activity; and<br>e) no soil is positioned where it may dam or divert<br>any river or stream or adversely affect instream<br>habitats, and<br>f) all bare soil areas are, as soon as practicable but<br>no later than six months from the date of<br>disturbance:<br>i) stabilised so that no earth moves off-site or<br>presents a danger to life or property; and<br>ii) vegetated, paved, metalled or built over, and<br>g) after reasonable mixing there is no conspicuous<br>change in the colour or visual clarity in any water<br>body or coastal water as a result of undertaking<br>the activity, and<br>h) all formation surfaces with an inward cross fall<br>are drained by a water table and cut-offs or<br>culverts are formed or installed so as to prevent<br>erosion of the formed surfaces, and<br>i) trenches formed for utility service lines are back<br>filled, compacted and revegetated as soon as<br>practicable, and<br>j) material used for fill is cleanfill material, and<br>k) soil is managed on the site during the<br>construction period and after, such that there are<br>no adverse effects on adjoining properties or any<br>waterbodies.|INr.54.2<br>Earthworks that contravene a<br>permitted condition are controlled if:<br>a) the maximum height or depth of<br>filling or excavation does not<br>exceed 4m, and<br>b) the site is not in the Land<br>Management Overlay, and<br>c) earthworks do not take place within<br>10m of the banks of any river<br>identified in Appendix 6 or within<br>20m of the Coastal Marine Area<br>except within the Port Operational<br>Area, and<br>d) no soil is positioned where it may<br>dam or divert any river or stream or<br>adversely affect instream habitats,<br>and<br>e) all bare soil areas are, as soon as<br>practicable but no later than six<br>months from the date of<br>disturbance, or the time specified in<br>the sedimentation and erosion<br>control plan for the site:<br>i)  stabilised so that no earth moves<br>off-site or presents a danger to<br>life or property; and<br>ii) vegetated, paved, metalled or<br>built over, and<br>f) all formation surfaces with an<br>inward cross fall are drained by a<br>water table, and cut-offs or culverts<br>are formed or installed so as to<br>prevent erosion of the formed<br>surfaces, and<br>g)   material used for fill is cleanfill<br>material.<br>Control reserved over:<br>i) loss of topsoil or movement of<br>soil down slope, and<br>ii) damage to structures or adjoining<br>properties, and<br>iii) soil and vegetation entering rivers<br>or coastal water, and<br>iv) damage to instream and coastal<br>habitats, and<br>v) adverse effects on catchment<br>stream flow, including<br>stormwater, and<br>vi) river bank and coastal erosion,<br>and<br>vii) duration of exposure of bare soil<br>to wind and rainfall, and<br>viii) water quality, including<br>suspended sediment load and<br>increased stream bed load, and<br>ix) the method and timing of the<br>activity, and<br>x) the area to be disturbed at any<br>one time, and<br>xi) the provision of structures to<br>control soil erosion or<br>sedimentation, and<br>xii) the timing and techniques used<br>for revegetation, and<br>xiii) the depth, height and volume of<br>cut and fill and the finished<br>ground level, and<br>xiv) the quality of fill material and<br>compaction methods, and<br>xv) visual effects, and<br>xvi)  control of noise, and<br>xvii)  control of dust, and<br>xviii)  traffic and access issues.|<br> <br>INr.54.3<br>Earthworks that contravene a controlled<br>standard other than g) are restricted<br>discretionary activities.  Where g) is<br>contravened the activity is a<br>discretionary activity.<br>Discretion restricted to:<br>i)<br>loss of topsoil or movement of soil<br>down slope, and<br>ii)<br>the potential for slope failure, and<br>iii) damage to structures or adjoining<br>properties, and<br>iv) soil and vegetation entering rivers<br>and coastal water, and<br>v) damage to instream and coastal<br>habitats, and<br>vi) adverse effects on catchment<br>stream flow, and<br>vii) bank and coastal erosion, and<br>viii) duration of bare soil to wind and<br>rainfall, and<br>ix) water quality, including suspended<br>sediment load and increased<br>stream bed load, and<br>x) the method and timing of the<br>activity, and<br>xi) the area to be cleared at any one<br>time, and<br>xii) the provision of structures to control<br>soil erosion or sedimentation, and<br>xiii) the timing and techniques used for<br>revegetation, and<br>xiv) the long term management of the<br>land cleared, and<br>xv) the provision of appropriate<br>resources to ensure that adverse<br>effects arising from emergency or<br>unforeseen circumstances are<br>controlled or mitigated, and<br>xvi) visual effects, and<br>xvii) the impact on privacy and on the<br>admission of daylight and sunlight<br>to neighbouring sites, and<br>xviii) in the case of earthworks within the<br>Landscape Overlays, compliance<br>with the objectives and<br>performance guidelines in<br>Appendix 7 (Guide for Subdivision<br>and Structures in the Landscape<br>Overlay), and<br>xix) Appendix 4 (marine ASCV overlay)<br>and Table 6.1 in Appendix 6<br>(riparian and coastal margin<br>overlays), and<br>xx) Appendix 9 (landscape<br>components and views), and<br>xxi) control of noise, and<br>xxii) control of dust, and<br>xxiii)  traffic and access issues.|



**10-44** **(12/11/12) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|INr.54A.4<br>In considering applications for landfills, Council will restrict its discretion to the<br>matters identified in INr.54A.3 provided that the application does not<br>contravene a restricted discretionary condition|INr.54A.5<br>Landfill development and operation are restricted discretionary<br>activities.  While landfills generally involve earthworks and modify the<br>shape of the land, their primary purpose is the disposal of solid waste.<br>The concentration of solid waste, often containing contaminants,<br>within landfill sites, increases the potential for adverse effects on the<br>environment beyond that associated with normal earthworks.<br>Additional adverse effects may include generation of leachate,<br>discharge of gas, geotechnical issues such as poor bearing strength<br>and settlement, and contamination of the land itself making it<br>unsuitable for other uses.<br>Some landfills operate as cleanfill sites, accepting only material that<br>does not undergo any physical, chemical, or biological transformations<br>likely to cause adverse environmental effects, or health effects, once it<br>is placed in the ground.  Cleanfill operations are clearly preferable to<br>activities accepting hazardous or potentially hazardous materials, and<br>are more likely to be granted resource consent.<br>Discharges to water and air from material within landfill sites also<br>require separate regional resource consents.|

**10-48** **(26/01/08) Nelson Resource Management Plan**


|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|INr.65.4 - INr.69.4<br>Refer to Assessment Criteria on preceding page|INr.68.5<br>Heritage Trees are trees for which retention is considered essential.  Landscape<br>Trees are trees for which retention is considered important.<br>Tighter controls are placed on Heritage Trees recognising that they are of<br>greater significance to the community than the Landscape Trees.<br>(note: section 330 of the Act provides for emergency works, such as the removal<br>of trees threatening life or property, but in strictly defined circumstance and by<br>certain persons or agencies.  Consent for such works can be applied for<br>retrospectively (section 330A)).  Some latitude is provided for the removal of<br>trees in the road reserve if it can be shown that it places an unreasonable<br>restriction on the roading network, recognising that the primary purpose of the<br>road reserve is transportation.|
|INr.65.4 - INr.69.4<br>Refer to Assessment Criteria on preceding page|INr.69.5<br>Local Trees are of noteworthy interest, and are not as significant as either<br>Heritage or Landscape Trees.  Retention and protection is encouraged.  A<br>week’s notice prior to removal of a Local Tree allows the Council the opportunity<br>to negotiate with the owner if it desires.  Written notice also allows the Council to<br>update its list of Local Trees.|
|INr.70.4<br>See Schedule Sch.M.|INr.70.5<br>See Schedule Sch.M.<br>The schedules for this Zone follow after the Rule Table.|
|INr.71.4<br>a) the location of the site in relation to the noise contour, and the<br>main source of the noise.<br>b) the number of people likely to be exposed to the noise, the type<br>of noise, and the duration of exposure.<br>c) the nature of the activity, and its susceptibility to noise.<br>d) the effectiveness of, and in particular the certainty provided by,<br>any conditions or controls that might be imposed on the activity.<br>e) the potential cumulative effects of an increased exposure to<br>noise.|INr.71.5<br>The rule is based on the predicted exposure of the site area within the overlay to<br>noise levels from the airport, on a long term basis.  The rule provides for<br>mitigation of potential adverse effects by the insulation of parts of buildings that<br>are most likely to be sensitive to noise.<br>The acoustic insulation standards in Appendix 19 provide one way of meeting<br>the permitted condition.  Alternative methods of meeting the standard can be<br>used, if certified by a suitably qualified acoustic engineer.|
|INr.71A.4<br>not applicable|INr.71A.5<br>The rule is based on the predicted exposure of the site are within the overlay to<br>noise levels from the Port Industrial Area. The rule provides for mitigation of<br>potential adverse effects by the insulation of parts of buildings that are most<br>likely to be sensitive to noise.<br>In order to ensure that the standard is met, certification of a suitably qualified and<br>experiences acoustic engineer is considered appropriate.|
|INr.72.4<br>In the case of discretionary applications, consideration will be given<br>to the nature of the activity and its likely sensitivity to the effects of<br>airport noise.|INr.72.5<br>The land between the Ldn 55-60 dBA (10.9 to 34.6 Pasques) noise contours is<br>unlikely to be exposed to airport noise to a great degree.  However, it is likely to<br>be subject to some noise nuisance and some recreational activities may be<br>affected.  This may help people decide the type of activities they establish in the<br>area, or whether they choose to incorporate acoustic insulation when they are<br>building.|

|**INr.73**<br>**Subdivision**<br>**– general**<br>**(except for**<br>**subdivision**<br>**in the**<br>**Services or**<br>**Heritage**<br>**Overlays)**|INr.73.1<br>Subdivision is<br>not a permitted<br>activity|INr.73.2<br>Any subdivision not located in the Services or Heritage Overlays is<br>controlled, if:<br>a) it complies in all respects with all the relevant standards in Appendices<br>10  to 12,  and<br>b) it complies with the mandatory matters in the Nelson Tasman Land<br>Development Manual 2019, and<br>c) esplanade reserves or strips as indicated in the Riparian Overlay of the<br>dimensions set out in Appendix 6, Table 6.2, are created and vested in<br>the Council, and<br>d) the minimum finished ground level for any land allotment (excluding<br>water bodies) is 15.35m NCC Datum, except in the Inundation Overlay,<br>and<br>e) the minimum finished ground level is greater than the crown level of the<br>road to which the piped stormwater from the allotment is drained,<br>except in the Inundation Overlay, and<br>f) every allotment is of a regular shape that will maximise the range and<br>efficiency of potential uses of the land, and<br>g) any existing buildings comply with the conditions for permitted activities,<br>or a resource consent, and<br>h) at the time of subdivision of any property adjoining the Nayland Road<br>South industrial/residential zone boundary, a buffer strip of at least 20m<br>in width is set aside, and a landscaped bund at least 3m high<br>constructed within it, along the section of the industrial/residential zone<br>boundary concerned.  Each section of earth bund shall be joined with<br>any existing sections of the bund so as to form a continuous barrier.<br>The buffer strip may, subject to encumbrances registered on the land<br>titles, be on either side of the industrial/residential zone boundary, or<br>may include land on both sides.<br>Control reserved over:<br>i) the matters contained in the Nelson Tasman Land Development<br>Manual 2019, and<br>ii) the effects of natural and other hazards, and<br>iii) design and layout of the subdivision, and<br>iv) protection of natural features, landscapes, heritage items and trees and<br>Maori values, and<br>v) riparian management, and<br>vi) public access, and<br>vii) adverse effects likely to arise from the subdivision, associated<br>development or subsequent use of the land, and<br>viii) development  of the subdivision and sites having regard to:<br>• <br>appropriate vehicle access, and<br>• <br>the intensity of buildings to be erected on each lot and the siting of such<br>buildings, and<br>• <br>provision of services, and<br>ix) stormwater management, and<br>x) the effects of vegetation clearance, land disturbance and earthworks,<br>including on visual amenity, soil erosion and sedimentation, and<br>xi) financial contributions in accordance with Chapter 6, and<br>xii) the future of land subdivided for the purposes  of public utilities and no<br>longer required for the purpose, and<br>xiii) in the Inundation Overlay, in addition to the matters listed above, control<br>is reserved over:<br>• <br>finished ground level, and<br>• <br>the nature of infill, its compaction and placement.|INr.73.3<br>Any subdivision not located in the<br>Services or Heritage Overlays that<br>contravenes a controlled standard is<br>discretionary if it is for the purposes of<br>a network utility. **industrial zone**






|AssessmentCriteria|Explanation|
|---|---|
|INr.73.4<br>a) the matters in the Nelson Tasman Land Development Manual 2019.<br>b) the extent of compliance with Appendices 10 to 12.<br>c) the extent of compliance with plan provisions relating to streams, drains leading to<br>streams, and any other waterbodies on the land to be subdivided.<br>d) effects on traffic, road network, access, parking, stormwater management, water<br>supply, sewage reticulation, and power and telecommunication services.<br>e) the extent to which the land is subject to natural hazards, or included in<br>inundation, floodpaths, fault areas and slope risk overlays, and whether any risks<br>can be remedied or mitigated.<br>f)<br>the pattern of subdivision and how it relates to the desired environmental<br>outcomes, amenity values for the locality, and efficient use of infrastructure.<br>g) the actual and legal protection of significant natural features or heritage items, and<br>means to avoid or mitigate significant changes to the landscape or amenity values<br>of the area.<br>h) the extent to which the proposal has regard to Maori values, particularly any<br>traditional, cultural, or spiritual aspect relating to the land.<br>i)<br>any consultation, including with tangata whenua as appropriate, and the outcome<br>of  that consultation.<br>j)<br>avoidance, remedy or mitigation of adverse effects of the subdivision, including<br>temporary effects of construction.<br>k) financial contributions (see Chapter 6).<br>l)<br>the development potential of other adjacent land.<br>m) the ground level required to avoid the effects of flooding.<br>n) the type of inundation likely to be experienced, whether it be stormwater ponding,<br>tidal inundation, or some other combination of circumstances which could lead to<br>surface flooding.<br>o) effects on neighbouring properties, especially stormwater runoff.<br>p) provision of adequate flow paths for surface flooding.<br>q) the possibility of an overloaded public storm water system overflowing onto<br>private property.<br>r)<br>effects of allotment size and shape, including on amenities of neighbourhood and<br>on the potential efficiency and range of uses of the land.<br>s) the values for esplanade purposes outlined in Table 6.1 or 6.2, Appendix 6,<br>including any additional information regarding the values of the reserve or strip<br>sought for the purposes outlined in section 229 of the Act.<br>t)<br>any circumstances which make the taking of the esplanade reserve or strip (or the<br>width stated in Appendix 6, Table 6.2) inappropriate, including (but not limited to)<br>the nature of existing development, reasons of security, public safety, minor<br>boundary adjustment.<br>u) any existing protection of the area including any existing esplanade reserves or<br>strips or any protective covenants.<br>v) alternative ways in which the esplanade values identified  in the area can be<br>provided for including (but not limited to) the use of esplanade strips and<br>protective covenants.<br>w) the assessment matters in Table DO6.1.1 regarding the type of protection<br>appropriate in given circumstances.<br>x) In the Nayland Road South industrial area, the extent to which industrial activities<br>could affect the amenity of adjoining residential sites.<br>y) The density of planting, mature height and species of plant proposed in any<br>required landscaping.|<br> <br>INr.73.5<br>Specific rules apply to subdivision activities proposed within<br>the Services and Heritage Overlays (see Rule INr.74 and<br>INr.75).<br>Subdivision is a controlled activity so that conditions can be<br>imposed on the development to ensure a satisfactory<br>standard of amenity, the minimisation of adverse effects and<br>that the site can be adequately serviced.<br>There is no minimum size for allotments, leaving this to the<br>market to determine.  Subdividers should note that the<br>proposed allotment should be capable of accommodating a<br>building or an activity which complies with the rules in this<br>Zone.<br>The controls also enable consideration to be had to the<br>development potential of nearby land, so that the level of<br>servicing provided is appropriate to the likely future demand<br>in the area.  This allows consideration of future roading<br>patterns, and demands on sewers and other services, to<br>avoid the need for costly and disruptive upgrading later.<br>The Act states the preservation of the natural character of the<br>river and coastal margins to be matters of national<br>importance.  This includes public access along these, and<br>protection of areas of significant indigenous flora and the<br>habitats of indigenous fauna, contained within them. It<br>provides a number of mechanisms to achieve this protection<br>including the taking of esplanade reserves and strips.<br>The river and coastal margins on the Planning Maps and in<br>Appendix 6, Table 6.2, have been identified as containing<br>riparian values in accord with section 229 of the Act. In some<br>cases riparian protection already exists, or special<br>circumstances exist, which make the taking of esplanade<br>reserves or strips unnecessary.  In other cases a lesser<br>width, or an alternative way of achieving riparian protection<br>may be more appropriate.  In these situations, a discretionary<br>consent application is needed, in order to depart from the<br>standards set out for a normal subdivision.<br>Where a subdivision is discretionary, and the allotment<br>adjoins any river or the coastal margin, then an esplanade<br>reserve or strip may be required as a condition of the<br>subdivision consent, having regard to the values identified in<br>Appendix 6, Table 6.1.<br>The minimum ground levels set are based on the best<br>estimates from the Ministry for the Environment for likely sea<br>level rise caused by global climate change.  This takes<br>account of predicted spring tides and expected tidal surges,<br>and their consequent effects on stormwater ponding.<br>Sites below the minimum levels stated for controlled activities<br>will be assessed individually to ensure that ground or floor<br>heights are sufficient to protect the site from inundation.<br>See Rule INr.54 (earthworks) where a site is being filled.<br>In the Nayland South industrial area, a special rule has been<br>imposed to ensure a landscaped bund is constructed when<br>subdivision occurs on land adjoining the residential zone.  A<br>similar subdivision rule has been imposed on the residential<br>zone.  The purpose of the landscaped bund is to ensure the<br>Nayland Road South industrial area can coexist alongside a<br>residential zone.|
